[1:0:204,43] 9658   Budget Stabilization Account  

[2:0:66,64] Proposition 2, approved by voters in November 2014, replaced the Proposition 58 (2004) version of the Budget Stabilization  

[2:1:66,74] Account (BSA) to build a stronger "rainy day" reserve while requiring accelerated debt pay down. Proposition 2 strengthened  

[2:2:66,84] the reserve by providing more stringent requirements to transfer funds back to the General Fund or suspend deposits to the  

[2:3:66,95] BSA, and increasing the reserve limit.  

[3:0:66,115] Proposition 2 requires a transfer from the General Fund to the BSA by October 1 of each year, as well as true up transfers  

[3:1:66,125] between the General Fund and the BSA for the two preceding fiscal years. In addition to the transfer to the BSA, a calculated  

[3:2:66,135] amount is appropriated for supplemental debt payments and other specified long-term liabilities.  

[4:0:66,162] LEGAL CITATIONS AND AUTHORITY  

[5:0:66,180] PROGRAM AUTHORITY  

[6:0:66,201] Section 20, Article XVI of the Constitution of the State of California.  

[6:1:66,211] Control Section 35.50, Budget Act.  

[7:0:66,229] Item 9658-011-0001, 2016 Budget Act and 2018 Budget Act.  

[8:0:66,249] Item 9658-012-1022, 2018 Budget Act and Government Code Section 16418.8.  

[9:0:66,286] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[10:0:66,304] 7760 - Proposition 2 requires the Legislature, through the 2029-30 fiscal year, to annually set aside in the BSA for a "rainy day"  

[10:1:66,315] 50 percent of the sum of 1.5 percent of estimated General Fund revenues and the amount of revenue from capital gains over 8  

[10:2:66,325] percent of General Fund tax proceeds that is not required to fund Proposition 98, and use the remaining 50 percent to pay  

[10:3:66,335] down debt. Beginning in 2030-31, 100 percent of the above sum would be deposited in the BSA for a "rainy day," reduced by  

[10:4:66,345] any amount up to 50 percent that the Legislature appropriates to pay down debt. The maximum balance in the BSA is limited to  

[10:5:66,355] 10 percent of General Fund proceeds of taxes for the fiscal year. Any amounts in excess of ten percent may only be used for  

[10:6:66,366] infrastructure needs.  

[11:0:66,386] Proposition 2 includes a true up mechanism for the two preceding years.  

[12:0:66,406] The Legislature may suspend or reduce the BSA transfer if the Governor declares a budget emergency. Withdrawal of funds  

[12:1:66,417] from the BSA is limited to half of the fund's balance unless funds in the BSA have been returned to the General Fund for  

[12:2:66,427] appropriation in the immediately preceding fiscal year.  

[13:0:66,447] Proposition 2 also establishes a Proposition 98 reserve whereby spikes in funding will be saved for future years. This will  

[13:1:66,457] smooth school spending and minimize future cuts. The Proposition 98 reserve does not change the Proposition 98 minimum  

[13:2:66,468] guarantee calculation.   See 9889 - Public School System Stabilization Account for more information on the Proposition 98  

[13:3:66,478] reserve.  

[14:0:66,518] FUND CONDITION STATEMENTS

[10:1:66,549] 7765 - EQUITY CLAIMS

[12:0:65,634] • Claims for which the appropriation made or fund designated is exhausted.  

[13:0:65,650] • Claims for which settlement is not otherwise provided for by statute or constitutional provision.

[14:1:66,678] Compensation and Government Claims Board in July 2016. The California Victim Compensation and Government Claims

[1:0:164,43] 9800   Augmentation for Employee Compensation  

[2:0:66,64] This item reflects funding augmentations for state employee compensation. If the Legislature previously appropriated money,  

[2:1:66,74] through this budget item, to pay for the economic terms of employee compensation in previous fiscal years, the funding for  

[2:2:66,84] those economic terms is included in departments' budgets. When economic terms require funding not yet appropriated by the  

[2:3:66,95] Legislature, those funds are included in this budget item.  

[3:0:66,115] Additionally, this item sets aside funding for penalties the state may face under the Affordable Care Act (ACA). Beginning in  

[3:1:66,125] 2015, the state became subject to the Employer Shared Responsibility provision of the ACA. This provision requires large  

[3:2:66,135] employers to offer health benefits to full-time employees, defined as those who work on average 130 or more hours per month  

[3:3:66,146] (or 30 hours per week), and their dependent children. Under this provision, the state may be subject to penalties (Part B  

[3:4:66,156] Penalty), which may include part-time, temporary, and seasonal employees that may have been considered full-time for one or  

[3:5:66,166] more months, were not offered or did not qualify for health benefits through the state, purchased health coverage from the  

[3:6:66,176] Health Insurance Marketplace (known as Covered California), and received a premium tax credit or cost sharing reduction.  

[4:0:66,197] The ACA also contains reporting requirements, which require the state to track specified ACA-related employee information on  

[4:1:66,207] a monthly basis to identify the employees who meet health eligibility requirements, document whether benefits were offered,  

[4:2:66,217] and whether the employee accepted benefits. This data collection is used to report the state's level of ACA compliance to the  

[4:3:66,227] Internal Revenue Service on an annual basis. The state may be assessed penalties for inaccurate reporting (Internal Revenue  

[4:4:66,237] Code sections 6721 and 6722).

[1:0:207,43] 9818   Federal Levy of State Funds  

[1:1:66,64] The federal courts periodically issue judgments or "writs of execution" against the State of California requiring the state to make  

[1:2:66,74] payments to the federal government. The writs and judgments provide the authority to the federal government to withdraw  

[1:3:66,84] funds from the state bank accounts maintained by the State Treasurer's Office at the various state depository banks.  

[1:4:66,105] Each year, the Budget Act authorizes the Department of Finance to identify specific appropriations or funds to charge when the  

[1:5:66,115] federal government withdraws funds from state bank accounts. When no specific appropriation or fund can be identified, the  

[1:6:66,125] withdrawals are charged to the unappropriated General Fund balance.  

[2:0:66,146] No levies were paid during the 2017-18 fiscal year and none have been paid through June 15, 2019.

[1:0:147,43] 9840   Augmentation for Contingencies or Emergencies

[1:3:66,84] appropriations, one for each fund type - General, special, and non-governmental cost funds. These appropriations are allocated  

[1:4:66,95] to other departments by the Department of Finance based upon the determination of need.

[1:0:168,43] 9885   Reserve for Liquidation of Encumbrances  

[2:0:66,64] For individual department budgets, encumbrances (commitments for the procurement of goods or services which have not yet  

[2:1:66,74] been received by the state) are accrued as expenditures by departments at year-end and included in the expenditure totals.  

[2:2:66,84] This treatment is in accordance with the budgetary/legal basis of accounting and consistent with individual department budgets.  

[3:0:66,105] For the purpose of determining the overall General Fund balance, Government Code Section 13307 requires that  

[4:0:66,115] encumbrances should not be counted as a budgetary expenditure until the delivery of the goods and services. Furthermore,  

[4:1:66,125] Generally Accepted Accounting Principles (GAAP) require that encumbrances be reflected as a reserve against the General  

[4:2:66,135] Fund balance and not as an expenditure, as in budgetary/legal basis accounting. Government Code Section 13306 and state  

[4:3:66,146] policy require compliance with GAAP whenever it is in the best interest of the state. This budget reflects a statewide adjustment  

[4:4:66,156] to reduce expenditures on a budgetary/legal basis by the encumbrance amounts to comply with Government Code Section  

[4:5:66,166] 13307 and GAAP. A reserve of fund balance for encumbrances for this same amount is shown in Summary Schedule 1 for the  

[4:6:66,176] General Fund.  

[5:0:66,197] COMPUTATION OF ENCUMBRANCE ADJUSTMENT  

[6:0:66,217] The State Controller's Office accumulated a preliminary estimated General Fund encumbrance total of $1,384,512,000 from  

[6:1:66,227] 2017-18 year-end financial statements submitted by state departments. For budgeting purposes, encumbrances are estimated  

[6:2:66,237] to be at the same level for the 2018-19 and 2019-20 fiscal years and are assumed to be liquidated (paid) within the next fiscal  

[6:3:66,248] year. The Encumbrance Adjustment Table summarizes the methodology and the calculation for the encumbrance adjustment.

[1:0:162,43] 9889   Public School System Stabilization Account  

[1:1:66,64] Proposition 2, approved by voters in November 2017, established the Public School System Stabilization Account (PSSSA) as  

[1:2:66,74] a ”rainy day“ reserve for K-14 schools.  

[2:0:66,92] Proposition 2 requires Proposition 98 General Fund deposits into or withdrawals from the fund each year, as well as two  

[2:1:66,102] preceding fiscal years, when specific criteria are met.   Calculation of a deposit or withdrawal from the   PSSSA does not change  

[2:2:66,112] the Proposition 98 minimum guarantee calculation.

[1:0:122,43] 9900   Statewide General Administrative Expenditures (Pro Rata)  

[2:0:66,64] Central service agencies, such as Department of Finance, the State Treasurer, the State Controller, and Legislature, provide  

[3:0:66,74] budgeting, banking, accounting, auditing, payroll, and other services to all state departments. The Pro Rata process apportions  

[3:1:66,84] the costs of providing central administrative services to all state departments and funding sources that benefit from the  

[4:0:66,95] services. Amounts apportioned to special funds for their fair share of central administrative services costs are transferred from  

[4:1:66,105] the special funds to the General Fund and the Central Service Cost Recovery Fund.  

[5:0:66,125] Prior to 2016-17, Pro Rata charges to special funds were normally included in the appropriate departmental budgets. This  

[5:1:66,135] budget item included Pro Rata costs directly charged to special funds for those cases where appropriate funding was not  

[6:0:66,146] provided for in departmental budgets. Effective 2016-17, this budget item includes Pro Rata costs charged directly at the fund  

[6:1:66,156] level, rather than each individual appropriation, pursuant to Government Code section 11274.
